    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer12714313961815329410"><b>In the tradition of <i>Go Ask Alice </i>and <i>Lucy in the Sky</i>, a harrowing account of anorexia and addiction.</b><br/><br/>She was a good girl from a good family, with everything she could want or need.   <span id="freeText12714313961815329410" style="display:none"><b>In the tradition of <i>Go Ask Alice </i>and <i>Lucy in the Sky</i>, a harrowing account of anorexia and addiction.</b><br /><br />She was a good girl from a good family, with everything she could want or need. But below the surface, she felt like she could never be good enough. Like she could never live up to the expectations that surrounded her. Like she couldn’t do anything to make a change.<br /><br />But there was one thing she could control completely: how much she ate. The less she ate, the better—stronger—she felt.<br /><br />But it’s a dangerous game, and there is such a thing as going too far…<br /><br />Her innermost thoughts and feelings are chronicled in the diary she left behind.</span>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1953102826" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953102826" />
    <a title="Petra-X" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x"><img alt="Petra-X" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603179398p2/1237196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953102826?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra-X" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra-X" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x">Petra-X</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=medicine-science">medicine-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=2017-100-reviews">2017-100-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=psycho-neurology-crime">psycho-neurology-crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953102826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14098965500524376972">Anorexia is the medium that carries the message in this book. It's not what kills the teenage diary writer, although she does die from it. <br/><br/>This book is built from cliches. One builds on another. Perhaps cliches are new and fresh to teenagers but those with years of reading behind them can see the next one coming. <br/><br/>The teenage diary writer, 'Ana' is from a newly-broken home. Her mother is fat, her father's new girlfriend is thin with big boobs  He gives her a car instead of love. Her best friend i</span>
  <span id="freeText14098965500524376972" style="display:none">Anorexia is the medium that carries the message in this book. It's not what kills the teenage diary writer, although she does die from it. <br /><br />This book is built from cliches. One builds on another. Perhaps cliches are new and fresh to teenagers but those with years of reading behind them can see the next one coming. <br /><br />The teenage diary writer, 'Ana' is from a newly-broken home. Her mother is fat, her father's new girlfriend is thin with big boobs  He gives her a car instead of love. Her best friend is, at her mother's encouragement, losing weight to get the lead part in a ballet. So they diet together. Best friend's brother whom she's known forever becomes a boyfriend, must be because of the way she looks, right? Then there is the sports coach who pays lip service to protecting the girls from anorexia. An only-second-best friend who is of course jealous, A size 2 dress that has to be got into, ana-mia sites online with seductive girls showing their ribs and boy-hips etc. It's a life where the only control Ana feels she has is over her own body and the better it looks (to her) the more the world will love her.<br /><br />The author is such a fake. She pretends that she is protecting her more vulnerable readers by never setting less than healthy limits. She starts 'Ana' and Jill off on 1,750 calories a day and has them reduce it to 1,250, it never goes beneath 1,000. The anorexics I knew were restricting themselves to 400 and 600 calories. The amount of food described in the diary does not add up to anything like 1,000 calories a day. Then there is the obsessive exercise and laxatives. The name of the tea in the book, Ballerina, is also a genuine slimmer's tea that is based on senna pods, a laxative. My grandma had two glasses by her bed at night, one for her teeth and one full of senna pods and water to keep her regular! <br /><br />Eventually 'Ana' overdoes it and collapses. Hospital etc follows but she cannot be kept in for long because the insurance won't cover it. She comes out and is determined to be healthy, but soon the lure of anorexia, of control, gets her again. More doctors. But they cannot help, nor can she be an inpatient because she doesn't have the insurance cover, even though her mother is a nurse in the same hospital. It's the same with therapists, there is no money to pay them, no insurance that will cover them, just group therapy which isn't intensive enough.<br /><br />Meanwhile her wealthy ballerina friend Jill has also collapsed from her extreme dieting. She is whisked off to an expensive clinic that specialises in teenage anorexics. <br /><br />I could go on, but you get the picture. At the end 'Ana' dies and Jill lives. They both suffered from anorexia but 'Ana' couldn't afford or get insurance to cover the treatment. Jill's wealthy family had the means to get the care that would heal their daughter.<br /><br />What killed 'Ana' was that medicine in the US is primarily a high-profit business, care and healing have to be purchased. If you can't pay, only the minimum is provided. Insurance companies are like a legalised mafia. Pay them 'protection' money and they will help you out when you need it. To a point. Further than that point they'll cut you off or... kill you. 'Ana' was too needy she had to die. <br />__________<br /><br />I've seen this book ascribed to the infamous Beatrice Sparks of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46799.Go_Ask_Alice" title="Go Ask Alice by Beatrice Sparks" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Ask Alice</a> fame. She didn't write it. Sparks would have been in her 90s when it was written - how much youth culture would she have been familiar with then - and dead a few years before it was published. She was also an ultra-conservative who saw everything in black and white. One step on the wrong path and it doesn't matter what you do, you are doomed. This book wasn't like that. Also although it wasn't well written it wasn't hilariously bad as Beatrice Sparks' books are.<br /><br />3.5 stars rounded down because the efforts at including steamy romance were puerile.<br /><br /><i>Rewritten July 2018 on a quick reread.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14098965500524376972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14406143720635182598">I have a love-hate relationship with this book.<br/>The book is very well written and obviously composed by someone with first hand views of an eating disorder's effect. Though at times, the symptoms of the main character are like many other novels surrounding anorexia - textbook examples. This is where the book is slightly unrealistic. Not every patient displays every symptom known to EDs. <br/>However, it remains that this book, especially when focusing on the family's reaction, is disturbingly accurate</span>
  <span id="freeText14406143720635182598" style="display:none">I have a love-hate relationship with this book.<br />The book is very well written and obviously composed by someone with first hand views of an eating disorder's effect. Though at times, the symptoms of the main character are like many other novels surrounding anorexia - textbook examples. This is where the book is slightly unrealistic. Not every patient displays every symptom known to EDs. <br />However, it remains that this book, especially when focusing on the family's reaction, is disturbingly accurate. <br />It's not a happy read, as I'm sure many who read the back will realize. It is also not a book that should be read by any recovering or recently recovered ED patients, as it is extremely triggering. My treatment group read this together, encouraging more than one relapse within the group of seven girls. I'm not sure how much I support teenage girls reading a book that encourages eating disorders to the unhealthy extent that "Letting Ana Go" does. It presents the false realities of anorexia as if they are rational (which is exactly how they appear in the patient's mind.) <br />I know this review is kind of all over the place, because as I mentioned in the beginning, I have such a love/hate relationship with the book. It is horrifyingly accurate and well-composed, which perhaps is what leads me to hate the content as I do.</span>

<div id="review_637126549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637126549" />
    <a title="Amanda Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4805959-amanda-johnson"><img alt="Amanda Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361485936p2/4805959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637126549?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Johnson" href="/user/show/4805959-amanda-johnson">Amanda Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637126549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5409820816419716216">Letting Ana Go is a book in the form of a diary that follows an unnamed teenage girl as she goes from a healthy athlete to someone in a desperate battle with anorexia. It is almost entirely in first-person, written as entries of the protagonist's diary that she received at the beginning of the book.<br/><br/>This was a refreshing format as most books I read and write follow the same formatting, and I was surprised at how well it worked. Letting Ana Go is brutally honest, allowing the reader an inside look</span>
  <span id="freeText5409820816419716216" style="display:none">Letting Ana Go is a book in the form of a diary that follows an unnamed teenage girl as she goes from a healthy athlete to someone in a desperate battle with anorexia. It is almost entirely in first-person, written as entries of the protagonist's diary that she received at the beginning of the book.<br /><br />This was a refreshing format as most books I read and write follow the same formatting, and I was surprised at how well it worked. Letting Ana Go is brutally honest, allowing the reader an inside look at what goes on inside the minds of these young women with the disease. It was scary how much I could actually empathize with this character and how easily it became for her to get swept into the world of anorexia. I went through devastating times similar to what this girl went through, and it made me wonder. Could this have been me? Could I, at some point in my life, actually get swept up in this disease too? She didn't even realize it, similar to the way actual girls with this disease don't realize it. I think the scariest, and saddest, part about this book is how real it is. Every single day, thousands of girls wake up with the same thoughts the protagonist of this book did. And every single day, many of them meet the same fate as well. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone who thinks they, or a loved one of theirs, maybe dealing with anorexia. Or even to someone who wants to learn more about how it affects someone. This book can truly open your eyes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5409820816419716216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_794375086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794375086" />
    <a title="Alexandra Bayer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12399851-alexandra-bayer"><img alt="Alexandra Bayer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589984237p2/12399851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794375086?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra Bayer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra Bayer" href="/user/show/12399851-alexandra-bayer">Alexandra Bayer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794375086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8568707927306581630"> She loved to run and was on her school's track team. She had a family and plenty of friends, and an eye on a nice boy. Everything was going well for her, until the day she had to start counting calories. Her coach wanted everyone to make sure they were getting the proper amount of calories, so she and her best friend, Jill, started watching together. Only problem was that Jill was a ballerina and wanted to slim down to get the part of Clara in The Nutcracker. Jill asked for support at the same </span>
  <span id="freeText8568707927306581630" style="display:none"> She loved to run and was on her school's track team. She had a family and plenty of friends, and an eye on a nice boy. Everything was going well for her, until the day she had to start counting calories. Her coach wanted everyone to make sure they were getting the proper amount of calories, so she and her best friend, Jill, started watching together. Only problem was that Jill was a ballerina and wanted to slim down to get the part of Clara in The Nutcracker. Jill asked for support at the same time as the main character's father left her overweight mother. Soon both girls were cutting back on calories and exercising like crazy. Nothing happened at first. They got compliments, she got a boyfriend, and she loved the way she looked, perhaps a bit too much. Soon things stated to spiral out of control, and as things worsened, the questions arises: what would you be willing to sacrifice in order to be beautiful?<br /><br /> This was the first fictional book I've ever read about anorexia. I was able to access it through PulseIt's 31 Days of Reading, and I am so glad I did. It was an extremely compelling book, and I finished it probably within 24 hours. It was written in the style of a diary, and the thoughts and stories recorded were very accurate with what an anorectic would put down. This story very clearly underlined the seriousness of this disease. It irritates me to no end when I hear people say that anorexia is a choice; anorexia is never a choice. Healthy people don't choose to starve themselves to look 'beautiful'. Anorexia is a lifelong struggle, and many people never get through it. I'm so happy this book was able to depict that fact.<br /><br /> This book was written in the format of a journal, so it was in first person. That could be part of the reason as to why I really enjoyed it: I love first person stories with characters that are easy to relate to. At the beginning of each entry, it gave the date and the main character's weight. Readers then have a visual every few pages (since the entries were usually quite short) to see her weight dropping. This was very helpful, because then it was much easier to keep track of how much weight was being lost. The look of the dialogue was very different than it looks in most other books. Instead of being in quotation marks, the person who was talking had their name written down, then a colon and their lines. It looked much like a script. The originality of the formatting was an interesting and enjoyable touch added to an already great read.<br /><br /> This book doesn't have a happy ending. I won't say exactly what happens, but if you don't like sad endings, don't read this book. Personally, I liked the fact that this book ended in a dramatic way. It drove the point home that anorexia is not a joke. This was the first book I've read in a long time that wasn't fantasy, because usually my favourite books are all fantasy. However, I could read it for free and had the time, so I started it out of sheer boredom. And then I couldn't put it down. I came home and read for several hours until I had finished it. The main character of this book can be compared to a train wreck: at first you don't see it coming; then you do, but there's no way to help. The main character was very personable and happy near the beginning of the book, a strong female lead. This story defined the gradual descent into the mindset of an eating disorder. If you have an eating disorder, read this novel. You will be able to compare your thoughts to this main character's, and see how she ended up. It may help you.<br /><br /> I thought this book was amazing. It's a much-needed dose of reality in a world of super-thin models and actresses, where images of unrealistic body types are splashed all over different types of media. I would rate this book a high four stars. It was a nice change from the rest of the books out there, and will stay in my mind for some time to come. If you enjoy reading about real-life problems, romance, and teenage issues, you should definitely read this story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8568707927306581630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16835201452298542597">Full disclosure: I only read this because I recently re-read Go Ask Alice and wanted to see if this could be as bad. Spoiler: Close, but not quite.<br/><br/>Aside from the middle-aged-woman-trying-to-sound-like-a-teen problem, there was the hey-I-read-a-magazine-article-on-anorexia-so-I'm-qualified-to-write-a-book-about-it issue.   <span id="freeText16835201452298542597" style="display:none">Full disclosure: I only read this because I recently re-read Go Ask Alice and wanted to see if this could be as bad. Spoiler: Close, but not quite.<br /><br />Aside from the middle-aged-woman-trying-to-sound-like-a-teen problem, there was the hey-I-read-a-magazine-article-on-anorexia-so-I'm-qualified-to-write-a-book-about-it issue. Bad. Just bad.<br /><br />Also, it included enough detail to be triggering without having enough depth to be helpful.<br /><br />Other minor notes: this is a lot more modern of a story than Go Ask Alice, but it's hilarious how the author tries to shoehorn in references to current/recent teen culture. "Hey, look, this book isn't from the 60s! I just talked about a TV show where the host makes fun of clips from the Internet! I am hip!"<br /><br />Also, for the amount of detail included in the book about what the main character ate and how how much she weighed and how many calories she allowed herself, parts just didn't make sense. Like, she would say that she was eating 1000-1200 calories per day and then how she threw away half of her salad that was just lettuce and tomatoes and that was all she was eating for lunch. I've lived on 1200 calories per day. It's not a lot but you still get to eat real food. The character talked more like she was eating 300 calories per day.<br /><br />Finally, the author seemed like she really, really hated My Fitness Pal, or some other similar calorie counting app.</span>

I couldn't put it down because I kept anticipating the end, but I DIDN'T KNOW IT ENDED LIKE <b>THAT!</b> <br/><br/>The fact that this book was written by 'Anonymous' and the main character remained anonymous just really hit it home that this is an issue many people go through.   <span id="freeText9061267171691593259" style="display:none">So, I picked up this book without reading the synopsis, or the back cover! <br />Probably one of the more depressing books I've read this year. It was so sad. I couldn't put it down because I kept anticipating the end, but I DIDN'T KNOW IT ENDED LIKE <b>THAT!</b> <br /><br />The fact that this book was written by 'Anonymous' and the main character remained anonymous just really hit it home that this is an issue many people go through. This book seemed so realistic, which just made it worse. I've read one other book that deals with anorexia, <i>Unbearable Lightness</i> by the lovely Portia de Rossi. Although that book really hit the heart as well since it was all true, I find myself having more sympathy almost for this character because she seemed to not be able to get the proper help she really needed.<br /><br />I have no idea why I like to torture myself by reading books like this. Just... If you're like me, make sure you wait to read this until you in a state of mind to handle it. It's awfully sad. Also, I had no idea this book was new until I picked out <i>The Perks of Being a Wallflower</i> reference, and checked the date. Might have to check out more of Anonymous' work!</span>

<div id="review_1287998687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1287998687" />
    <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona"><img alt="Michelle Wrona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576510116p2/15162465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1287998687?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Wrona" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona">Michelle Wrona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=2015-favourites">2015-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=awesome-ending">awesome-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=made-me-fangirl">made-me-fangirl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=i-feel-it-in-the-heart">i-feel-it-in-the-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=death-sickness">death-sickness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=sad-depressing-read">sad-depressing-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=too-good">too-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1287998687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15312483790518024235">This review can also be found on <a href='http://thatgirlybookworm.blogspot.ca' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Thousand Lives Lived,</a> check it out for more!<br/><br/><b> *4.5 star rating* </b><br/><br/><b>You know, I've always seen these books around at the bookstore. <i>Go Ask Alice</i> has been on my TBR for ages. Ages, literally. <i>Letting Ana Go</i> was actually one that I never even heard about until my local library's catalogue received it. Anorexia is a sensitive subject that not many modern YA novels touch upon on excluding Laurie Halse Anderson's <i>Wintergirls,</i> a favourite of mine. This anonymous author ha</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15312483790518024235" style="display:none">This review can also be found on <a href="http://thatgirlybookworm.blogspot.ca" rel="nofollow noopener">A Thousand Lives Lived,</a> check it out for more!<br><br><b> *4.5 star rating* </b><br><br><b>You know, I've always seen these books around at the bookstore. <i>Go Ask Alice</i> has been on my TBR for ages. Ages, literally. <i>Letting Ana Go</i> was actually one that I never even heard about until my local library's catalogue received it. Anorexia is a sensitive subject that not many modern YA novels touch upon on excluding Laurie Halse Anderson's <i>Wintergirls,</i> a favourite of mine. This anonymous author has hit it perfectly, in a tiny novel that keeps readers guessing.</b><br><br>I love making predictions when reading. Not every novel can obviously leave you with an endless amount of questions that surround the protagonist or plot, but this sure did. Although it has an unattractive cover, the title and premise sounded so relatable (not to me, but to teenagers everywhere) and I found myself in the mood for a novel that's just surrounded with <b>one thing.</b> After reading, I've come to realize that the author adds more than just an anorexic character; there are many more issues including divorce, keeping fit and drinking at a young age. Go multi subjects!<br><br><blockquote>"Me: I feel like I am my best friend. When I'm able to get through a meal without eating too much, there's this thing I feel inside of me—this strength. It's like a place of power, and when I don't eat too much, or when I exercise enough, it makes me feel invincible. It keeps me company." (Hardcover, page 228)</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437235547ra/15555009.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that I even think about it, this title doesn't even seem to make sense, unless the heroine's name is Ana. Through the end of the novel where the protagonist goes through an even tougher situation, her name even gets <b>blacked out</b> and she seems to have no identity. And at the same time, all of the characters are just classified by their first name. When things get hectic by the end, everyone is just by their name. <b>IS THIS NON-FICTION? IS THIS REAL? WHAT? WHOA.</b> If I found it to be actual non-fiction, I'd totally shriek because it's a total crazy story. My life depends on knowing the truth. *stays determined*<br><br><b>You'd think that this has a pretty easy plot, but it doesn't.</b> This book is surely complex. The author makes TWO girls anorexic and it starts off small, just wanting to lose a few pounds and some body fat. But eventually, it becomes like an addiction, probably something even like taking drugs. Your whole mindset is suddenly changed and your life just depends on getting skinnier and skinnier. And then eventually, you have no more goals for yourself and you just collapse. Sure, a diet can be helpful for some, but starving yourself? This is completely ironic because the heroine even told her mother that she had to organize her meals correctly, but then all she's eating is rice cakes. O_O<br><br><b>The writing of this book was utterly fabulous.</b> It was simple, easy-going and easy to follow. A lot of these stories have all of these complications where everyone's trying to help the troubled character out and it just gets chaotic. Because we had an independent young teen as our main character, she kind of blew all of the troubles out and sticked to her own plan. These kinds of books have a broad message that everyone just wants to help out with in reality. I bet that raising awareness for anorexia and eating healthy in a healthy way is the most effective when a person reads a fictional story that deals with the subject. <i>Letting Ana Go</i> left that impact on me and I'm now afraid to eat less than I'm supposed to. *grins*<br><br>PLOT TWISTS? SUSPENSE? A MAD ENDING? You've got it. <b>I never saw that coming, I'll tell you that.</b> I totally got freaked out in the end and was completely shocked. Yeah, picture an "O" shaped mouth on my face.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437235547ra/15555010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Heck yes, I need all of the books that are written in this tradition.</b> I'll just head to my local bookstore, grab a basket, and slide all of the books off the shelf and head to the cashier, not even caring how much it'll cost me or affect my book buying ban. I can't get enough of this book and the romance and practically EVERYTHING. The perks of being a teenager and having troubles? This is it, and shows that every single teenager has some kind of issue, with some people having a bigger one than others. This is one of the realest contemporaries that I've ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15312483790518024235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1015499869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1015499869" />
    <a title="Amy M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3932759-amy-m"><img alt="Amy M" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1015499869?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy M" href="/user/show/3932759-amy-m">Amy M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1015499869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11724083211189462553">I loved "Go Ask Alice" when I was a teenager, so I was excited to see this YA book at Target. However, I was pretty disappointed. I felt that Ana, while a pretty realistic character, did not accurately portray anorexia. First of all, she only lost 20 or so pounds, down from 130, so the numbers were not shocking. The whole story took place over less than a year, and generally young bodies can endure much longer. I wish the author had given Ana more symptoms, and described them in more detail (for</span>
  <span id="freeText11724083211189462553" style="display:none">I loved "Go Ask Alice" when I was a teenager, so I was excited to see this YA book at Target. However, I was pretty disappointed. I felt that Ana, while a pretty realistic character, did not accurately portray anorexia. First of all, she only lost 20 or so pounds, down from 130, so the numbers were not shocking. The whole story took place over less than a year, and generally young bodies can endure much longer. I wish the author had given Ana more symptoms, and described them in more detail (for example, the dark downy hair she grew at the end of the book was just mentioned but not discussed by her doctors), and that they had gone into more detail about the clinic she stayed at for a short time. <br /><br />However, I do think it's good to get information out about anorexia so that symptoms can be recognized. That being said, this book could be dangerous for girls who are teetering on the brink of an eating disorder…I don't think death is a deterrent for many. They just see the allure of being thin and being in control.<br /><br />A quick read and probably a good book for the parents of pre-teen and teenage girls who are at risk to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11724083211189462553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_587235469" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/587235469" />
    <a title="Sarah Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie"><img alt="Sarah Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589089368p2/6515737.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/587235469?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Marie" href="/user/show/6515737-sarah-marie">Sarah Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=some-people-die">some-people-die</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=my-eyes-bled">my-eyes-bled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6515737-sarah-marie?shelf=enough-drama-to-make-a-soap-opera">enough-drama-to-make-a-soap-opera</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587235469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16054929304831094621"><u>Letting Ana Go</u> by Anonymous<br/><br/><b>1.5 stars</b><br/><br/><p>Ana is a good girl and she feels as though she’s not good enough for the perfect façade her family presents to the public. The one thing Ana knows she can control is her eating. Ana is spiraling, but she’s not eating it’s the best she’s felt in a long time. I remember loving Go Ask Alice in middle school; it’s one of the books that I consider to be a part of my childhood favorites. When I saw the this was free on Simon Pulse It I jumped to read it (that’s how </p></span>
  <span id="freeText16054929304831094621" style="display:none"><u>Letting Ana Go</u> by Anonymous<br /><br /><b>1.5 stars</b><br /><br /><p>Ana is a good girl and she feels as though she’s not good enough for the perfect façade her family presents to the public. The one thing Ana knows she can control is her eating. Ana is spiraling, but she’s not eating it’s the best she’s felt in a long time. I remember loving Go Ask Alice in middle school; it’s one of the books that I consider to be a part of my childhood favorites. When I saw the this was free on Simon Pulse It I jumped to read it (that’s how long ago it’s been- there isn’t even a Simon Pulse It, now it’s called Riveted) and I instantly disliked Ana. Ana is my biggest problem with this novel and that isn’t a good thing when the novel is a diary. At first, Ana is a normal girl with good, healthy eating habits- until Ana’s best friend and her “perfect” mom make a comment about Ana losing a little more weight. She starves herself because her friend said it would be FUN. This is a horrible example of eating habits and disorders to display to younger audiences. Naturally, she runs all the time even though she has no fuel in her body- goes to rehab- then collapses and dies- the typical “anonymous” storyline. I’m sorry but this a pile of crap and after two year of ruminating on this it’s one of those novels I forget about, but once I remember it I’m angry. It left a bad taste in my mouth. These type of storylines make it seem like eating disorders have no chance of recovery and overcoming the problem; using death to display tragedy after multiple failed rehabilitation or attempts at intervention is not a positive message to send to younger readers. Also Ana was a completely judgmental twat to her mom and it only fueled my dislike for her and this “novel”.</p><br /><br /><b>Whimsical Writing Scale: 2<br /><br />Kick-Butt Heroine Scale: 1<br /><br />Villain Scale: 2 (very disappointed with the depiction of eating disorders)<br /><br />Character Scale: 1<br /><br />Plotastic Scale: 1</b><br /><br /><p>Overall, I suggest skipping over this one. It’s a newer anonymous novel so I don’t consider it to be a classic or necessary for your angsty teen reads (there’s better stuff out there). I suggest Wintergirls by Laurie Halse Anderson instead because it’s a beautiful novel that portrays eating disorders in a stark, gut-wrenching story that has stayed with me since my middle school years.</p><br /><br /><b>Cover Thoughts: Typical anonymous cover with half a face in the dark. Bleh. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16054929304831094621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_514079816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514079816" />
    <a title="Andrea Diaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5857345-andrea-diaz"><img alt="Andrea Diaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356574238p2/5857345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514079816?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Diaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Diaz" href="/user/show/5857345-andrea-diaz">Andrea Diaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514079816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14802041973124725841"> <a href='http://literarygetaway.blogspot.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353696i/707018.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>This book was amazing. It took me deeper into the world of anorexia. I know people who have suffered from eating disorders, myself being one of them, but never really knew what went through the mind of a person suffering with anorexia. Ana keeps a food diary given to her by her cross country coach and tracks her weight and the day's events. At the beginning, you see her weight stay within a 5 pound range, between 130 and 135, which is healthy for a girl of her height (5'7"). Through the st</span>
  <span id="freeText14802041973124725841" style="display:none"> <a href="http://literarygetaway.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353696i/707018.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>This book was amazing. It took me deeper into the world of anorexia. I know people who have suffered from eating disorders, myself being one of them, but never really knew what went through the mind of a person suffering with anorexia. Ana keeps a food diary given to her by her cross country coach and tracks her weight and the day's events. At the beginning, you see her weight stay within a 5 pound range, between 130 and 135, which is healthy for a girl of her height (5'7"). Through the story, she gains a love interest and teams up with her best friend, Jill, in restricting their calories. They become obsessed with exercise, low calorie budgets, and weighing themselves every day. <br><br>While reading "Letting Ana Go", I was exposed to the wonders of hip bones, thigh gaps, and rib cages. Apparently you can only be beautiful if you have all of these characteristics present. That's what Ana and Jill had themselves believing.<br><br>I feel that this is a must read for everyone, not just teen girls. Parents should especially read it. They need to know that to many girls, looks are everything and they will go to great lengths to achieve the ultimate body. This book is a sure tear jerker. It took me on a ride. I absolutely loved everything about it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14802041973124725841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer813292613&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813292613" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1315918330097899973">This book was good in terms with educating people about anorexia, however I think it lacked something in its format. I've read the previous books in the series (Go Ask Alice, Jay's Journal, & Lucy in The Sky) and they all share the same basic format of a diary written by an anonymous teen. While the other three (especially the former two) do a good job of making you believe you're actually reading a diary, this one falls short. It seems more like just bad writing. You could definitely see the st</span>
  <span id="freeText1315918330097899973" style="display:none">This book was good in terms with educating people about anorexia, however I think it lacked something in its format. I've read the previous books in the series (Go Ask Alice, Jay's Journal, &amp; Lucy in The Sky) and they all share the same basic format of a diary written by an anonymous teen. While the other three (especially the former two) do a good job of making you believe you're actually reading a diary, this one falls short. It seems more like just bad writing. You could definitely see the story line but it wasn't believable that the narrator was actually writing it down. It just made something seem lost. Because of this, a lot that happens feels less personal, or shocking I guess and I walked away feeling just kind of "meh" about it. SPOILERS: However, I think it does mention a lot of very accurate and important things about dealing with anorexia nervosa, such as briefly mentioning how the narrator's insurance won't cover her medical bills and how that negatively affects her recovery, and how some small comments and habits of those around can build up to very negative self esteem and self destructive behaviors. I just wish they had stayed more true to the previous books' formats though so I could have a better understanding/connection with the narrator. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1315918330097899973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1055525999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055525999" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3052319-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555615313p2/3052319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055525999?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/3052319-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3052319-heather?shelf=ya-and-under">ya-and-under</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3052319-heather?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3052319-heather?shelf=2014-just-books">2014-just-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3052319-heather?shelf=realistic">realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3052319-heather?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055525999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8129937750257122610">I had read Go Ask Alice a couple years ago and decided to try out another book from the other "Anonymous" author collection. I am so glad I did. Like Go Ask Alice, this is the main character's journal, which started off as a food/feeling journal. It is interesting to see what she wrote, her weight changes, and the evolution of her disorder. Also, interesting, because it was a journal, we never know her name - really who writes their name in their journal entries?? But for the remainder of the re</span>
  <span id="freeText8129937750257122610" style="display:none">I had read Go Ask Alice a couple years ago and decided to try out another book from the other "Anonymous" author collection. I am so glad I did. Like Go Ask Alice, this is the main character's journal, which started off as a food/feeling journal. It is interesting to see what she wrote, her weight changes, and the evolution of her disorder. Also, interesting, because it was a journal, we never know her name - really who writes their name in their journal entries?? But for the remainder of the review I'll just call her Ana - for simplicity. <br /><br />This book gave me so many different feelings - I just wasn't expecting it. I find eating disorder books very interesting and very relatable since I had an eating problem when I was a teenager (not a full-out eating disorder but I believe it was borderline). I found that the topic was handled very well and covered all the ups and downs of the disorder – how it starts, the actual issue, and all the ugly.<br /><br />All the characters were written very realistically. I believed everything that was going on and how each individual reacted to Ana and her behaviour. I completely felt for Jack! It must be hard standing there watching people you love hurt themselves. I could relate to Ana and her entire situation (although I have not experienced it all). Unlike what the back of the book describes, she did not start out by wanting to lose weight, but her sport forced the girls to track all the food and exercise they did. This was actually one of the parts of the books that completely irritated me! Why was it only the girls, yes it is predominantly girls who have eating disorders but why just focus on them? If you’re worried about eating disorders and are going to force people to track what they are doing (which I believe would just cause disorders instead of stopping them) then make the entire team do it not just the girls! Also, the coach’s reaction to Ana cutting her calories and losing weight just irritated me – if that’s how you are going to react the whole exercise was for nothing!<br /><br />I was completely surprised by the ending and didn’t fully no how to react. I wasn’t expecting it – although I should have. Do not go into this expecting anything or having a certain mindset. It will throw you for a loop!<br /><br />I would recommend this if you’re interested in eating disorders, Go Ask Alice style, journal writing, or realistic fiction. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8129937750257122610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_634236057" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634236057" />
    <a title="Van (Short &amp; Sweet Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3043015-van-short-sweet-reviews"><img alt="Van (Short &amp; Sweet Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513312582p2/3043015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634236057?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Van (Short &amp; Sweet Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Van (Short &amp; Sweet Reviews)" href="/user/show/3043015-van-short-sweet-reviews">Van (Short &amp; Sweet Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634236057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18205787583574551942">This is my first ‘Anonymous’ book, having never read any of the other similar books published in the previous years (Go Ask Alice, Lucy in the Sky or Jay’s Journal). LETTING ANA GO is the diary of a 16-year-old girl chronicling how a simple task of keeping a food journal for track turned into an uncontrollable obsession to be thin. At the beginning of each journal entry Ana jots down her weight trying to retain the daily suggested 2,200 calories intake. As the story progresses, Ana’s best friend</span>
  <span id="freeText18205787583574551942" style="display:none">This is my first ‘Anonymous’ book, having never read any of the other similar books published in the previous years (Go Ask Alice, Lucy in the Sky or Jay’s Journal). LETTING ANA GO is the diary of a 16-year-old girl chronicling how a simple task of keeping a food journal for track turned into an uncontrollable obsession to be thin. At the beginning of each journal entry Ana jots down her weight trying to retain the daily suggested 2,200 calories intake. As the story progresses, Ana’s best friend Jill convinces her to start losing weight with her. Ana’s usual 2, 2000 calories went down to 1,700 calories, 1,200 and then 1,000 calories a day. <br /><br />LETTING ANA GO gives readers a glimpse into the mind of someone who suffers with anorexia nervosa, a person who loses weight that would be consider unhealthy for their age and height. I don’t know anyone that suffered an eating disorder, but this book shows how easily and scary a person can develop an eating disorder and not know it. It was sad to see how far Ana, and her friend Jill went to obtain the ‘model’ figure. This is a real problem that many women have suffered for a long time, thanks to the media, magazines, and celebrities some women believe that in order to be considered beautiful they need to weight a certain amount, or their waistline needs to be certain size, etc. Ana’s account is very real and disturbing, and though she’s blinded by her own actions…it was also heartbreaking to see everyone that loved her unable to help her. Her parents checked her into a rehab facility, hoping that she’d get better and her boyfriend would always tell her how much he loved her and how beautiful she was but it was never enough. <br /><br />LETTING ANA GO is an amazing and at the same time heartbreaking story. It highlights the issue of anorexia and how it can become an obsessive-addiction that can lead to serious health consequences. The ending had me floored. I was completely in shock. I don’t really remember how I expected it to end, perhaps a happy ending like most book but I guess the way it ended made sense. This is a book everyone should read, not just teens. This book is the type of book that will stay with you long after you read it, I’m really glad I got the chance to read it. <br /><br />*I received a review copy from the publicist and in exchange I provided a honest review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18205787583574551942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1074046111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074046111" />
    <a title="Ms. Yingling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2636606-ms-yingling"><img alt="Ms. Yingling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376174508p2/2636606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074046111?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Yingling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Yingling" href="/user/show/2636606-ms-yingling">Ms. Yingling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074046111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3273997348066272648">When her cross country coach makes her keep a food diary to make sure that she and the other girls on the team keep up their calorie counts and DON'T descend into an eating disorder, our unnamed character starts to lose weight. Her best friend, Jill, is a ballerina on a dangerously restrictive diet, and her mother has gained weight and is given a hard time about it by her father. When her father ends up leaving her mother for another woman, and she starts to run faster times after losing about t</span>
  <span id="freeText3273997348066272648" style="display:none">When her cross country coach makes her keep a food diary to make sure that she and the other girls on the team keep up their calorie counts and DON'T descend into an eating disorder, our unnamed character starts to lose weight. Her best friend, Jill, is a ballerina on a dangerously restrictive diet, and her mother has gained weight and is given a hard time about it by her father. When her father ends up leaving her mother for another woman, and she starts to run faster times after losing about ten pounds, she starts to work with her friend on ridiculously low calorie amounts. This brings her the attention of a boy she likes, and she's determined to lose weight to get into a size two dress, even though she is 5'7". Vanessa, another girl on the team, is worried about her, but she attributes that to jealously. After collapsing at a meet, she has to bring her weight up, her mother starts working days in order to be with her, and her friends watch her more closely, but she is now struggling with anorexia and finds it hard to break the cycle. Her friend Jill is hospitalized, as is she, and she does gain weight for a while, but the book has a very sad ending. <br />Strengths: My readers are already craving a lot of problem novels-- this doesn't usually occur until deep into February! This was a good read, along the lines of The Best Little Girl in the World. There is some kissing and touching, but nothing too bad. <br />Weaknesses: I was bothered that this is an "anonymous" diary, when you know it was written by an adult somewhere. It's just too specific and message heavy to have been a real diary. I also wish there had been some information at the back of the book about eating disorder support. <br /><br />I struggle with giving girls books about eating disorders, but in 17 years of teaching, I have only had two girls who had to go into treatment. In the one case, the girl came to my attention BECAUSE she was reading so many books about the topic, and she is doing better now. This book certainly didn't make an eating disorder look in any way attractive, although the fact that the father left the mother in part because of her weight (or at least that was her daughter's perception) was a bit alarming.) At any rate, a good spring board for discussion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3273997348066272648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67702928-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606107711p2/67702928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2459049055?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/67702928-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781442472136" href="/book/show/16074891-letting-ana-go">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67702928-hannah?shelf=the-woooooooooooorst">the-woooooooooooorst</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2459049055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3363970660228527068">Ohhhh dear, this was such a mess. I was expecting it to be, but not to the degree it ended up being. This is an extremely triggering book and shouldn’t be read by young teens, which is ironically the target demographic. <br/><br/>Anorexia and eating disorders are much more complex than this book makes them out to be. I would have liked for there to be a disclaimer, or a page of resources like in <i>The Book of David</i>. But neither of those things were included, so instead we get a poorly-written teenager’s str</span>
  <span id="freeText3363970660228527068" style="display:none">Ohhhh dear, this was such a mess. I was expecting it to be, but not to the degree it ended up being. This is an extremely triggering book and shouldn’t be read by young teens, which is ironically the target demographic. <br /><br />Anorexia and eating disorders are much more complex than this book makes them out to be. I would have liked for there to be a disclaimer, or a page of resources like in <i>The Book of David</i>. But neither of those things were included, so instead we get a poorly-written teenager’s struggle with her weight. I don’t suffer from an eating disorder, but I trust the reviewers on this site who do, and if they say this book is trash and inaccurate, then I’m going to believe them. Research seems to be a foreign concept to the people who write these books, which is detrimental to their purpose to educate and can have negative consequences.<br /><br />Aside from that, there’s not much I can say that I haven’t said about the other books I’ve read that are “in the tradition of” Beatrice Sparks’s ilk. The characters are flat, the story is boring, the writing is inconsistent, the boyfriend was extremely misguided and selfish, and no one bothered to do a Google search to fix inaccuracies. (I highly doubt a divorce would be finalized in less than a month.) Sometimes the main character uses complex phrases, and then she turns around and says things like, “Boobalicious the office manager.” How can I take this book seriously when I read things like that? <br /><br />This is probably the worst one I’ve read so far, considering the subject matter. I only recommend it if you’re a completionist and want to read all these terrible accounts. It’s hard to get through and the imagery is pretty graphic, so go in with caution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3363970660228527068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_695873694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/695873694" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22060873-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381801755p2/22060873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/695873694?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/22060873-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695873694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12951852766474225841">To be honest I don't know where to start about this book. Just the fact that it was written by an anonymous authour just makes you so much more intrigued to read it. I myself have struggled with anorexia nervosa since the age of 11 and just seeing that what I felt and thought happens to a lot of people sure made me feel like I wasn't the odd one out. Unlike many things that revolve around the topic of anorexia, such as blog posts, this book was not triggering at all. If anything, it made me feel</span>
  <span id="freeText12951852766474225841" style="display:none">To be honest I don't know where to start about this book. Just the fact that it was written by an anonymous authour just makes you so much more intrigued to read it. I myself have struggled with anorexia nervosa since the age of 11 and just seeing that what I felt and thought happens to a lot of people sure made me feel like I wasn't the odd one out. Unlike many things that revolve around the topic of anorexia, such as blog posts, this book was not triggering at all. If anything, it made me feel stronger about recovering.<br /><br />This is just one of those books that will change the way that you look at things forever. Wether you have struggled with the disease or not, it is a lesson that can be applied to any aspect of your life. It taught me that the most important thing isn't "being" beautiful, it's feeling beautiful on the inside which is all that could ever matter. Because once you love yourself everyone around you will do the same.<br /><br />"Ana" was just an average girl, with average height and weight. At first, you can tell that she is very athletic, but doesn't show much concern with GAINING weight. On the other hand her best friend Jill is encouraged by her mother to "stay thin". After agreeing to accompany Jill on her diet, "Ana" sees herself trapped, by the constant obsession over restricting food.<br /><br />Everything just goes too far, but "Ana" never seems to notice. She believes that no one will love her if she is "fat". But those thoughts and the actions that came with them, ruined her until the point where it was too late.<br /><br />I absolutely recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12951852766474225841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1174811158?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " class="user" itemprop="url" name="PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps " href="/user/show/8149327-pinkamy-loves-books-cats-and-naps">PinkAmy loves books, cats and naps </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18975745-letting-ana-go">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1174811158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11168819756997645560">Everything in Her (unnamed) life was perfect, until Her dad left home, probably because Her mother was too fat. She begins a diet with Her best friend, Jill, which, due to other unaddressed stressors in Her life, turns into anorexia. <br/><br/>LETTING ANA GO, written in diary format, follows Her slow plunge from first place runner to anorexia. A lot of the diary entries were repetitive and boring, day after day of her weight, calories and dieting just isn't that interesting. LETTING ANA GO does a great jo</span>
  <span id="freeText11168819756997645560" style="display:none">Everything in Her (unnamed) life was perfect, until Her dad left home, probably because Her mother was too fat. She begins a diet with Her best friend, Jill, which, due to other unaddressed stressors in Her life, turns into anorexia. <br /><br />LETTING ANA GO, written in diary format, follows Her slow plunge from first place runner to anorexia. A lot of the diary entries were repetitive and boring, day after day of her weight, calories and dieting just isn't that interesting. LETTING ANA GO does a great job showing the subtle changes in Her thinking and behavior, and is probably how a lot of teens with eating disorders feel. Obsessing about food and weight is tedious and repetitive, because that's a component of the illness. Anonymous could have done a better job with pacing, which finally picked up during the last 30% and ended strong. The ending was the best part of the story.<br /><br />I'm not sure I'd recommend LETTING ANA GO to girls suffering from eating disorders, reading about food, calories and weight can't be helpful. Once She is diagnosed, there are helpful warnings, but these aren't anything teens don't already know. Parents worried about their children might get some insights into their thinking, but that's about it. The only reason for two stars instead of one is the strong ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11168819756997645560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2031245707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2031245707" />
    <a title="Elise Kiwaki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68663968-elise-kiwaki"><img alt="Elise Kiwaki" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2031245707?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise Kiwaki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise Kiwaki" href="/user/show/68663968-elise-kiwaki">Elise Kiwaki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2031245707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4327815506983753309">I picked up this novel and expected to read a simple story about a young girl struggling with an eating disorder, but what I got was far from my initial assumption. I found this book to be quite insightful about how eating disorders affects a healthy mind and how influence plays a huge role in this process of manipulation. I like how the novel is written like it is the diary, specifically a food diary, of the main character, Pam, and how the author of this novel uses this to their advantage to s</span>
  <span id="freeText4327815506983753309" style="display:none">I picked up this novel and expected to read a simple story about a young girl struggling with an eating disorder, but what I got was far from my initial assumption. I found this book to be quite insightful about how eating disorders affects a healthy mind and how influence plays a huge role in this process of manipulation. I like how the novel is written like it is the diary, specifically a food diary, of the main character, Pam, and how the author of this novel uses this to their advantage to show us the speed at which Pam loses herself to the idea of being perfect. Reading this novel, I slowly began to realise how many people could be influenced by their peers, friends, and family into an eating disorder. In this novel Pam has a best friend who is an avid ballet dancer. We immediately take notice by the way Pam describes her best friend, Jill, that she may have an eating disorder considering the amount of time she obsesses over her weight and body image. Pam was influenced by Jill to start dieting; nothing harmful in doing so. However, the situation began to escalate quickly, and in a matter of a few ten pages or so, it is obvious to the reader that Pam and Jill were going down a dangerous path. The author did a tremendous job of interpreting to the reader the emotional and physical struggles Pam went through while Anorexia Nervosa took over her mind. While reading, there was no point where I felt that the author decided to add "filling" into their writing so that it would appeal to the audience and/or try to decrease the probability of dissatisfied readers. In fact, I believe that the author wrote this piece mainly for the awareness of our toxic society. By the end the of book you are left with multiple questions unanswered, and possibly you may feel a little uneasy. There is no possible way that you can read this book without having to check your own morals and where your heart lies; I know I had to. Reading this book was like a walk through a grave yard; it's not easy and it certainly is not fun. However, it allowed me to feel more sympathy towards those who do struggle with an eating disorder and I was able to learn more about the process of it all. As hard as this book was to read because of how it accurately described the effect of eating disorders on the mind, I do recommend people to read it for themselves. It is better to have some knowledge than none, whether that knowledge scars you or not. I do warn those who are currently struggling or have recently recovered from an eating disorder to read this novel with caution. This novel does not beat around the bush, and could possibly trigger an individual struggling or have struggled with an eating disorder. I would like to see a book like this in a high-school curriculum, mainly because I feel that numerous people start to have eating disorders during their high-school years, and by having awareness books likes this one, we could possibly prevent some individuals from losing themselves like Pam has. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4327815506983753309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C6TzLRQgrtFl499lDrFh1zPklW2nYLeaXHLGWGLxr+lZ8ea9QZIDgjOngK7gcixL8rw/3a6uhE2v5LGsu92ZHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7WaE5U2FN9sceC0h/4dumfYmofaukB05Yhhg9UbUw46/M5F1GDeaiEo8cuoRRCMFN34LRqdeLu6RjhcBn/j1eg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
